< Text>
Rented here over a year, and the staff has always been helpful and friendly.  I recently added another unit, and currently have both a drive-up and a inside unit and would recommend this facility wholeheartedly.

The units are always clean when given to you (after that, it's all on you), there's no bug or rodent infestations, and I've never had water incursion.   It's probably not approved, but I put in a lightbulb-to-outlet adapter in my drive-up unit so I could plug in a small shopvac and keep down the dust that my stuff seems to attract (asthma).

I've had people help me with moving things in and out, and the office staff are always watchful and attentive to who is going in and out.  It's not just that my drive-up unit is visible from the office windows, but they seem to watch the monitors too and there's cameras pointed down every corridor and at every wall of doors.

< Review>
Came in about 2 months ago for a consultation, staff is very friendly every single time and always greeted me with a smile. Had to come back several times because Dr. Wong wanted to make sure my readings are as accurate as it can be. I had very high astigmatism and didn't think i would be a candidate for the surgery. I got really excited when i found out that i can get the Lasik procedure done.

The office and equipments used are very clean which is always comforting. They have a Keurig and a water dispenser for everyone to consume while you wait which was never long.

<Text>My first impression was the appointment making and confirmation process. They also let me know how long the appointment was to take and what to expect. The phone call was easy and there were no issues there. I appreciated the text and email reminders with the address listed.
The next experience I had with Lasik vision was the day of my free consultation.  The building was what I would expect on the outside, but I was hoping for a more ‚Äúclinical‚Äù or ‚Äúmedical‚Äù feel on the inside.  I didn‚Äôt get this sense though. It felt more like a salon! There were about 3-4 girls sitting up front at the reception desk (I think at best this area was made for two). The fact that there were so many ladies wasn‚Äôt so much of an issue, but the chatter was. It just didn‚Äôt come across as professional.  This is why I mentioned it had a ‚Äúsalon‚Äù feel.
I got evaluated by an assistant to start. She did some scans and test to look at the shape of my eye and the surface area moisture. You could tell she was used to the same routine over and over.  She mentioned to me that my cornea was thinner than they would like to do Lasik and so they would probably recommend another procedure (that uses the same laser) that took more recovery time (but as more appropriate for my situation).
I was moved to an eye exam office and waited about 20 minutes for the doctor to arrive. I was next door to the room where they discuss the financial side and wrap up the consultation. While I was in this room waiting, I was able to overhear quite a bit of two different things going on.
The first thing I heard was a potential patient wrapping up her consultation and discussing it with the sales person. Something that I noted was the price she mentioned and the word ‚Äúgroupon‚Äù. Another thing I heard was an assessment where I heard the assistant pretty much tell the next customer the same exact thing that they told me.  Routine speech that did not sound customized to the patient, and the associate sounded seriously bored and disinterested.

The doctor did some tests and told me more about why they would recommend the PRK surgery rather than the standard Lasik. The doctor was friendly enough, but I couldn‚Äôt help but feel that the whole thing was all about the ‚Äúsell‚Äù.
When I finally went to the last office for the salesperson to wrap things up, she basically summarized what the doctor said and asked me if I had any questions. My first question was price.  I was quoted $1700 for one eye, or just under $2000 if I wanted the service that included the ‚Äúplugs‚Äù for my tear ducts (to keep eyes hydrated after surgery) and for a guarantee on the surgery that I could return to get it done again if I ever needed it in the future.
I went home and looked up this business on groupon. Lo and behold, they are on there.  Groupon was advertising Lasik for $699 (one eye). This was about what I heard them quote the lady when I overheard their conversation.  There are a couple of issues I have with this.  Firstly, I understand that I was recommended for PRK which was a slightly different version of Lasik, I can‚Äôt imagine why though the price would suddenly jump from $699 per eye to $2000! This leads me to my second point. I don‚Äôt like it when businesses do this (quote a much higher price for a service they offer on groupon for less).  This has happened to me before (ironically with a salon which I compared this place to).  My last and third point is that being on Groupon is a HUGE deterrent for me from using Lasik Vision Institute.  This is a medical procedure and pretty serious (considering it affects one of the major senses and is in an area with major amounts of nerve endings).
I also looked up the doctor who would be performing the surgery after this whole experience. At best she has ‚Äúmixed‚Äù reviews. Some good; but some quite bad.
I still want to get my vision corrected with Lasik. Just not with Lasik Vision institute.<//Text>< user>

<Review>I had my surgery done almost a month ago and should have reviews sooner! My eyes were terrible before the surgery. I got PRK which the doctors and staff told me would be a tough recovery compared to normal lasik. They answered all the questions I had about anything relating to the surgery. I had about 3 appointments before the actual surgery day. Everyone there is extremely nice and caring about their customers.
As for recovery I am doing great now. Apparently larger prescription they correct, the more time it takes for your eyes to stabilize. So I have periods of slight blurriness and near perfect vision throughout the day. After the first week, I had my first follow-up appt. I had 20/20 then which was pretty amazing. Of course initial few days after the surgery my eyes felt like someone put hot sauce in them. But I was prescribed vicodin and 3 types of eye drops to help with the pain and recovery. Over the past month, my eyes have been getting more and more stable. As I write this my vision is just barely blurry, but about an hour ago it was probably better than 20/20. After the first 10 days I was driving myself easily.
I still accidentally try to pull off my glasses when I am going to wash my face or anytime I normally would. And then I get so happy I don't wear glasses haha. I definitely have to wear sunglasses outside and for the first week inside too, just because light sensitivity. I can probably handle not wearing sunglasses outside. I never did that while I had glasses and now I realize that I should have been wearing them outside anyways.
I paid for the groupon which was about 1400 for both eyes. But I opted in for all the extra things such as tear plugs, warranty on the surgery, and some new software that makes the eye surgery slightly better. <Rate>5<//Rate>< Review>
Website is awesome. It reallly gives you an instant professional look with professional capabilities all of the banks have. The marketing staff that helps you market yourself on other platforms is second to none. It's like having your own free marketing consultant. Ours has optimized our facebook and linked in pages and is awesome. But the problem is that we got the 220 website specifically as a way to stay in touch with our realtors and past clients through email drip campaigns. We were so excited to be able to do drip campaigns off of it and automatically send the stay in touch newsletter. Then, after paying, we were heartbroken to learn that everyone had to opt in to get our emails. Unlike Mail Chimp, which sends the email with an opt out at the bottom, our folks would have to opt in. Only 17 out of 169 did, making the email function useless. We had envisioned building drip campaigns for every stage of the loan process, including our new leads. Forget it. Impossible to get them to opt in. We are now back to mail chimp. It's maddening. I write this review not to be mean, but in hopes that they will change the opt-in policy to an opt out policy. Until then, count your 220 website useless for email drip campaigns. Also, of the few who did opt in, the 220 monthly email seems to go into their junk mail, so they don't see it anyway. GRRRRR!  Update: After reading this review, 220 moved all our contacts over from 220 to mailchimp for free. (There is normally a fee for that.) We have an appointment scheduled with our marketing consultant to learn how to send the 220 monthly email using mailchimp. Wish we could send it directly through the site, but the workaround isn't bad.</Review>

<review>Came here on Sunday morning - it is spacious and we got seated right away.
We ordered the bun bo hue and the pho #3.

The bun bo hue was delicious! I would come back here just for this noodle soup again. It looked like it wasn't as rich and flavorful as usual, but when we tried it- it was a really light but flavorful broth. Most bun bo hues have lots of spice, but in this one you could taste the broth and had the perfect level of spice.

The pho was pretty good as well. The noodles weren't as chewy as I would like, but the broth was good and all the meats were also quite good. It came with soft tendons and fatty meat slices, which I don't normally each but we're good.

Parking is available on the street - we didn't have any trouble when we went and got a spot across the street.
Prices are also reasonable with $8-9/bowl.<//review>< gmap_id>

I've been to numerous Pho spots and this place just sticks out to me the most. Their rice dishes are super delicious!!! They use this crispy bacon pieces (not bacon bits) as a topping in their rice dishes alongside with green onions and fish sauce, it enhances the dish to the extreme. Not many Vietnamese places do this so if you do drop by, definitely order and try one of their rice plates.</Review>

< Review>
Overview: Food is okay. Reminiscent of old Kevin's Noodle House location nearby that recently closed. Service staff is friendly. Details below.

Food: The food is pretty standard. Menu offers little choices in the way of vegetarian or pure seafood options. Only one menu item out of 70 or so offers shrimp, no other seafood to be found. Pho is standard, tasted the same after eating it five times now. When the restaurant does something just okay, but does that thing consistently, all one can really praise is consistency.

Price point: standard price point, but could be better for the food offered.

Atmosphere: sort of dim lighting, restaurant does not feel clean.

Service: staff is friendly. Does not check in on you, but does fill up water.<//Review>

<user>113770411529025960850< /user><user_name>Seng Saeliew<//user_name>< time>
1554792257072<//time>
<rating>4< /rating><review>There isn't many pho restaurants that can get a 5 star since many restaurants do not have a turn over rate that the noodles and ingredients are usually average to below par quality. With that being said, Pho Ao Sen has a decent turnover rate   meaning there is always fresh ingredients on hand. Good pho are hard to come by and hard to recommend since the quality varies by the time of the day. Best eaten before 3 pm after that, what ever is left is left and that will sit for however long it takes until the nest customer makes a request for a bowl of pho. When compared to the other surrounding pho restaurants, this location serve up a better version of the pho bowl in many instance. There is plenty of seating inside the establishment for everyone and the menu is extensive but I personally still recommend their more popular dishes as the turnover rate is higher. If you're ever in the area and craving for pho, drop by this joint and request for an extra large pho bowl and maybe a triple color drink to go along with that for a balance meal.< /review>< pictures>

< Review>
Pho An San is better than any pho that I've had in San Francisco!

The broth screams flavor.  It's so flavorful in fact that I did not need to color my broth red and brown or ask for more lime.  That's a first!

Tip: The rare steak quality is superb!  To take advantage of this, order pho with the rare steak on the side.  They don't charge for this service (some places do *cough Pho 2000*) and you can prevent your beef from becoming overcooked.  However, note that the amount of beef you get is the same whether you order a large or regular.  Deceptive eh?</Review>

< text>
Updating review as of Jan 2020.  Ao Sen is till run by the same family/folks as it was +5 yrs ago.  Food quality/prep is still pretty much top notch. Def come here for their signature dishes that are hard to find elsewhere - the bun cha Ha Noi (grilled pork patties and slices marinated in a sweet salty sauce with mildly pickled mango and carrots done basically as good as you might find in north Vietnam), and the cha ca Thang Long - hot plate pieces of sweet white fish (large, juicy, moist, not at all over cooked) marinated with dill served with traditional sides (can't think of another Viet restaurant around that has this on their menu)!  Place can get noisy when it's packed, and maybe minor wait time if you come during peak lunch hours.

original review -
Great food, staff can be off with service given how busy they get, be ready to wait if you come during busy time.</text>

< user_name>

<Date>1459815651926</Date><Rating>3</Rating><Review>Food: 4.5 stars
Cleanliness: 3
Service: 2 stars
I've been coming to this place for years and always like their food. Their old location nearby Lake Merritt had more a homey feeling to it. Now the new location looks more like an overpriced Vietnamese restaurant. However, the quality of their food has remained consistent. Good choices are the beef pho, grilled pork vermicelli and the Hanoi vermicelli. Rice plates are good alternate choices. However they suffer from skimpy portion syndrome and you could end up going home hungry.
A big plus is I hardly suffer from dry mouth and headaches after eating at this place. My guess is there's less MSG in their food.
The dining area is clean for the most part. And tables are cleaned up right away after the customer leaves. Areas for improvement are the bathroom and parking lot areas.
Service quality for the most part is average and acceptable. Workers are fast and efficient. Sometimes young workers tend to get caught up in coversations with their own or their own smart phone. Warning: workers speak little or no English at all potentially screwing up your order.
My biggest pet peeve is workers, including the owner, NEVER say thank you. Did I say the owner. These include situations like leaving a good tip in front of THEIR face. I supposed this is a common experience in most Vietnamese restaurants. I wonder if there's even a word for thank you in Vietnamese.
A reminder if this is going to be your first visit: PAY AT THE CASHIER after you eat. There's no visible sign anywhere. And remember your table number. You don't want to pay for somebody else's bill.< /Review><Pictures>None</Pictures>< response>
None</response>
